<Date>1525928759788</Date><rate>5<//rate><review>My boyfriend and I love going to Growler's Sub Shack! Upon our first visit we actually got to meet the owner who is a really nice guy. He's a veteran, and a local, small business owner. (Big fan of supporting local!) The place is clean and charming, the staff are very friendly and helpful, and at the end of it all- the food is great! Lots of variety of sandwiches, chili fries, salads, soups, and more. We stop all the time to get these tasty gourmet sandwiches (we love the meatball sub, the sausage sub, and the cheesesteak ones) on our way to outdoor adventures, or for just a "picnic" at home. It's in a great location and is worth a visit! Forget the big chain sandwich shops and give a taste to some of the best sammies I've tried in a long time a try! <Review>High-end Chinese fusion in Agoura Hills? I'm in!

Mandarin Lotus is located right off the 101 freeway on Kanan Road. I never knew this place existed until my friend started raving about it a few weekends ago at the Chili Cook Off. Based on what she said, I knew I needed to go check it out. I was not disappointed.

To my surprise, this restaurant was established in 1988. Formerly known as Mandarin Express, this restaurant specializes in Michelin-inspired Eurasian cuisine, with unique molecular gastronomy techniques and recipes. Fusion recipes include tastes from many cuisines, including French, Spanish, and Thai, to name a few. Their ingredients are definitely high quality and fresh.

I've been here a couple times now, and both times were excellent. This is definitely elevated Chinese cuisine, and they have very interesting items on the menu. Their menu is actually huge, with countless options to choose from ranging from low price to very expensive high-end. I've only been for lunch, so I've only gone cheap with the broccoli beef lunch special, but I am curious about a number of their other items. I will say, the broccoli beef is very good here, and the rice is cooked to perfection.

If you've never been, I'd definitely say this is a worthwhile restaurant to visit if you're in the area. Service is very nice, but maybe not the quickest. They do cook all of their food fresh to order, so this isn't much of a complaint, just a heads up to those in a rush. Due to the proximity to my office, I'll likely be back soon. Go ahead and give it a try for yourself!< /Review><Pictures>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipN0B2D1ZKoeTU4YWWcmmI55DaSBvulnqIJcqHP8=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipN4SzmQWGU_l4PPzcuDhlbXH9cdWA1n-l2nafJL=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOdTIc_KMsmK1VXgVCSA5xUsDo0mgsZq3gagzVD=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]< /Pictures>< resp>

Dan and Kim are incredibly nice and friendly people. A week ago my husband and I were traveling through Calabasas from Las Vegas, NV and fortunately found Mandarin Lotus. The food was fresh, healthy, delicious.... actually very very delicious! We called in and placed an order for pick up, when we arrived Dan met us near the entrance and greeted us personally. <username>Darth Rad< /username><time>1239951364205</time><rate>5< /rate><Review>So, this is my seventh year living in Oak Park, and the first time that I've been to this amazing hole in the wall restaurant!    I'd always been vaguely aware of this nondescript restaurant - it's squeezed in a tiny space in a strip mall,  near the karate center, Nick Rail's music,  behind the IHOP, and way behind the Jack in the Box at the corner of Kanan and the 101 off-ramp.  I guess it was the "Express" in the name which made me think it was something like "Panda Express" - take out pseudo-Chinese junk food.  Or maybe it was the small restaurant space and buffet-like store counter which you can see through the front windows, also reminiscent of a fast food take out restaurant.  Panda Express it most definitely is not.  Mandarin Express is of all things a fancy gourmet restaurant!   Chinese-Mediterranean-Californian fusion food.   They take some basic Chinese food ingredients and cook it with a variety of vegetables and spices from around the world. You can eat an all-vegetarian meal here!  There's an entire page of mock duck/chicken/shrimp/pork dishes.   But their shrimp and other meat dishes are terrific too.  The food just bursts with multiple flavors in your mouth.  I really think they should re-name the place, or at least take out the "Express" part from the name.  It just doesn't do the place justice.  The owner-cooks are really friendly too.  A great place to take your best friends and family!< /Review><pics>None<//pics><Resp>None</Resp><Gmap_id>0x80e826ab6e3b9443:0xb12aabb77ef4d1b3<//Gmap_id></record>

<Rating>5< /Rating><Review>My son went here a lot when he lived in the area. So he chose it for his birthday dinner. When we got there it was obvious the owners knew him and had missed him. They asked about one of his friends that had passed away. In fact everyone that came in that night gave and received personal and warm greetings. It was like a family gathering.

What could inspire such happiness beyond cordial friendliness?

The food! It was close your eyes and luxuriate awesome!

While my son and I noticed changes to the orange chicken, it was still delicious. This is not a static restaurant. It's fusion. They learn and incorporate from a variety of food cultures. So the OC (which BTW we never found in China) they reimagined was great - no skimping on anything.

We tried the shrimp they recommended but declined to eat it shell and all (if you've been to China you know about exoskeleton delicacies - a taste we haven't acquired). But even though we took off the shells, the seasoning was too incredible not to nibble off from the usually discarded shell. And the seasoning on the included vegetables led to who gets the last one squabbles.

Mongo beef - great. Cashew chicken- great. Chicken fried rice - ok anywhere else but with how everything else was spiced to perfection it suffered by comparison but was still enjoyable.

There were many other artistic and culinary touches that enhanced the food experience. This is not a decor destination. This is about the food and people dedicated to their craft and growing with it. And genuinely loving it.

My wif and I loved it too. It's now on our list to return in a month for a date night.

I hope you'll try it and love it too.

Be seeing you!< /Review>< Pictures>
None<//Pictures>

1585443059787</time>
< Rate>
3<//Rate>
< Review>
The worst part about this location honestly is the pricing, even for a single player looking to get some time on a table to practice. The only redeeming quality is the fact that the equipment is very nice-both tables and house cues. However, given its location, it doesn't seem like there is much of a scarcity of patrons on any given evening, so I don't expect the pricing to come down anytime soon...

Haven't tried the food, but I never see anyone here eating and from the looks of the menu, it truly seems like more would be desired, especially given the price range of table time.

It is definitely a nice hangout spot for a group of friends, family-friendly atmosphere for sure, and in general I would recommend this place to have a fun time. But be aware that pricing for table time increases as the number of people present in a group at any one table increases.< /Review>

I got tired of being deafened by loud, annoying bar music and drunken bros in PB so I took to the streets searching for a better pool place. This spot's very comfortable and has plenty of felt (I've never had to wait for an open table). The place seems to be asian run, and most of their clientele is as well (which made me feel slightly uncomfortable on first visit- being the only white guy there), but they turned out to be quite friendly and inviting. I highly recommend popping in if you're looking for a slightly quieter spot where you can actually hear another person from across the table.< /Text>

< review>
Some distance to major highways, and this charger is definitely for local apartment dwellers or small business employees while shopping at the Target area. Not being stereotypical, to own a Tesla and charge the car overnight at home is the quality way to go and should be planned financially and lifestylely. Stalls are fully occupied quickly around 11:30 on weekend. The only feeling good thing is it's easier to maneuver cars here than the Cupertino location. Still there are many ICE and Teslas wandering around along with Target's 18 wheelers and other delivery trucks. Charging currents are mostly on the low side but still faster than other DCFC. Save the hassle and enjoy a quality time with your family at other places. I certainly welcome more Superchargers, simply for more options when needed! Ought to replace half the gas station pumps with chargers.</review>

< text>
I went to iGeek Tech Repair and unfortunately I did not really get my laptop repaired. It was an somewhat an Mac Pro that had perhaps damage on the touchpad so moving the mouse was difficult and hard at times. I knew that I probably could fix it by getting a repair tool kit myself from the internet and doing it myself which would have costed me 30 dollars but I wanted to see if professionals could do it for faster and cheaper. Although I commend the staff for maintaining professional standards, the feedback I heard back from them was extremely vague about what was the issue. Perhaps I did not give them enough time but I needed the laptop back by a certain date. I given them one day and a half to hopefully fix my laptop. I given my laptop on a Friday afternoon but I needed it back my Monday morning for school work.

I tried calling them back and they said they couldn't find the issue but I needed my Mac back so I went to get it back on Sunday afternoon. The touchpad was still glitchy at times and I knew that it was not completely fixed.
Here is my complaint:
The problem wasn't that my laptop didn't get fixed. It was the problem that they charged me a whole 50 dollars as service fee for just opening it up and not repairing it at all. Now I would have been fine if they reduced it down to maybe 20 or even 25 dollars (because they didn't repair anything). But a whole 50 dollars seems too extreme to me for just opening up a laptop and not explaining the details of why they could not repair the touchpad or even figuring out the issue with it. Now keep it mind I would have paid the 50 dollars if they would able to provide a professional checkup worksheet of perhaps what parts were damaged or perhaps explain to me properly what the issue really was. However, they just said that they could not figure things out and just said to me I needed to pay the 50 dollars and I could have my laptop back.

Now I would maybe give them the benefit of the doubt and say that they do not work with macs that often since mac have a reputation for being hard to repair. I would understand that. But in reality I am just writing this review to show that I had a horrible experience and not all experiences are 5 stars as others. I would say that if you are a windows laptop user, you would probably be fine since those are easier to repair than macs. However, if you are a mac user, you are really taking a 50/50 gamble on this place maybe.< /text>
